<li><a href="/wiki/KRS-One#Stop_the_Violence_Movement" title="KRS-One">Stop the Violence Movement</a></li>
<li>H.E.A.L. Human Education Against Lies</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Def_Squad" title="Def Squad">Def Squad</a> (honorary member)<sup id="cite_ref-hdd_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdd-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></li>

</div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mclyte.com">mclyte<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Lana Michele Moorer</b> (born October 11, 1970), better known by her stage name <b>MC Lyte,</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Rap_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap music">rapper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disc_jockey" title="Disc jockey">DJ</a>, and entrepreneur. Considered one of the pioneers of female rap,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> MC Lyte first gained fame in the late 1980s, becoming the first female rapper to release a full solo album with 1988's critically acclaimed <i><a href="/wiki/Lyte_as_a_Rock" title="Lyte as a Rock">Lyte as a Rock</a>.</i> The album spawned the singles "<a href="/wiki/10%25_Dis" title="10% Dis">10% Dis</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Paper_Thin_(MC_Lyte_song)" title="Paper Thin (MC Lyte song)">Paper Thin</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stone_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stone-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 1989, she joined the <a href="/wiki/Supergroup_(music)" title="Supergroup (music)">supergroup</a> <a href="/wiki/Stop_the_Violence" class="mw-redirect" title="Stop the Violence">Stop the Violence Movement</a>, and appeared on the single "<a href="/wiki/Self_Destruction" title="Self Destruction">Self Destruction</a>", which was the inaugural number-one single on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_Rap_Singles" class="mw-redirect" title="Billboard Hot Rap Singles"><i>Billboard</i> Hot Rap Singles</a> chart.
</p><p>Her second album <i><a href="/wiki/Eyes_on_This" title="Eyes on This">Eyes on This</a></i> (1989), included the single "<a href="/wiki/Cha_Cha_Cha_(MC_Lyte_song)" title="Cha Cha Cha (MC Lyte song)">Cha Cha Cha</a>". In 1991, MC Lyte released the hit single "<a href="/wiki/Poor_Georgie" title="Poor Georgie">Poor Georgie</a>", which marked her first appearance on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>. Her 1993 single "<a href="/wiki/Ruffneck_(song)" title="Ruffneck (song)">Ruffneck</a>", made her the first solo woman rapper to achieve a <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_certification" title="Music recording certification">gold certification</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 1994, she collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a> on the song "<a href="/wiki/You_Want_This" title="You Want This">You Want This</a>", and was featured alongside <a href="/wiki/Queen_Latifah" title="Queen Latifah">Queen Latifah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yo-Yo_(rapper)" title="Yo-Yo (rapper)">Yo-Yo</a> on the remix track "<a href="/wiki/I_Wanna_Be_Down#Hip_hop_remix" title="I Wanna Be Down">I Wanna Be Down</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Brandy_Norwood" title="Brandy Norwood">Brandy</a>. Her 1996 single "<a href="/wiki/Keep_On,_Keepin%27_On_(MC_Lyte_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Keep On, Keepin&#39; On (MC Lyte song)">Keep On, Keepin' On</a>" featuring <a href="/wiki/Xscape_(group)" title="Xscape (group)">Xscape</a>, reached the top ten on <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100. She then collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a> on the hit song "<a href="/wiki/Cold_Rock_a_Party" title="Cold Rock a Party">Cold Rock a Party</a>", which would become her fifth number-one song on the Hot Rap Singles chart. In <a href="/wiki/46th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="46th Annual Grammy Awards">2004</a>, she was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Rap_Solo_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Rap Solo Performance">Grammy Award for Best Female Rap Solo Performance</a> for the track "<a href="/wiki/Ride_Wit_Me_(MC_Lyte_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ride Wit Me (MC Lyte song)">Ride Wit Me</a>".
</p><p>Throughout her career, MC Lyte had collaborations with mainstream artists such as <a href="/wiki/Sin%C3%A9ad_O%27Connor" title="Sinéad O&#39;Connor">Sinéad O'Connor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Will_Smith" title="Will Smith">Will Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moby" title="Moby">Moby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aerosmith" title="Aerosmith">Aerosmith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a>; and has been cited as an influence to many women in hip hop. <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> &amp; <i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a></i> ranked her as one of the 50 greatest rappers (2023).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> She has received the "I Am Hip Hop" Icon Lifetime Achievement from the <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a>, and was honored at the <a href="/wiki/Hip_Hop_Honors" title="Hip Hop Honors">VH1 Hip Hop Honors</a>. On October 2014, Lyte become the first female artist to perform Hip Hop at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In September 2016 she was awarded with the <a href="/wiki/W._E._B._Du_Bois_Medal" class="mw-redirect" title="W. E. B. Du Bois Medal">W. E. B. Du Bois Medal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>'s highest honor in the field of African and African-American studies.<sup id="cite_ref-hu_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hu-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In addition to her career as a rapper, she has worked in parallel as voiceover talent for various events, writer, <a href="/wiki/Disc_jockey" title="Disc jockey">DJ</a> and has starred in various roles in film and television. In 2022 has her directional debut with the short film <i>Break Up In Love</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Lyte has also worked with several charities, including her own foundation, <i>Hip Hop Sisters</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Grimm_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grimm-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Lana Michele Moorer</b> was raised in the East Flatbush section of <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, New York City. She began <a href="/wiki/Rapper" class="mw-redirect" title="Rapper">rapping</a> at the age of 12.<sup id="cite_ref-first_ladies_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first_ladies-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> MC Lyte's original stage name was Sparkle.<sup id="cite_ref-halftimeinterview_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-halftimeinterview-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> She began recording her first track at age 14, although it took two years before it was able to be released.<sup id="cite_ref-clip_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clip-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 1">&#58;&#8202;1&#8202;</span></sup>
</p><p>She regards <a href="/wiki/Milk_Dee" class="mw-redirect" title="Milk Dee">Milk Dee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Audio_Two" title="Audio Two">DJ Giz</a>, the hip hop duo <a href="/wiki/Audio_Two" title="Audio Two">Audio Two</a>, as "totally like [her] brothers", because the three grew up together. Audio Two's father, Nat Robinson, started a label for them called <a href="/wiki/First_Priority_Music" title="First Priority Music">First Priority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-halftimeinterview_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-halftimeinterview-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> After making the label, Robinson cut a deal with <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic</a> under a condition that Lyte would get a record contract with Atlantic as well.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_career">Musical career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Musical career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Beginnings:_Lyte_as_a_Rock_and_Eyes_on_This_.281987.E2.80.931990.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings:_Lyte_as_a_Rock_and_Eyes_on_This_(1987–1990)">Beginnings: <i>Lyte as a Rock</i> and <i>Eyes on This</i> (1987–1990)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Beginnings: Lyte as a Rock and Eyes on This (1987–1990)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1987, at the age of 16,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Lyte released her debut single, "<a href="/wiki/I_Cram_to_Understand_U_(Sam)" title="I Cram to Understand U (Sam)">I Cram to Understand U (Sam)</a>", being one of the first songs written about the <a href="/wiki/Crack_epidemic_in_the_United_States" title="Crack epidemic in the United States">crack era</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> She was 12 years old at the time she wrote the song.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Firehouse_Studios_1988.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Firehouse_Studios_1988.JPG/220px-Firehouse_Studios_1988.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Firehouse_Studios_1988.JPG/330px-Firehouse_Studios_1988.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Firehouse_Studios_1988.JPG/440px-Firehouse_Studios_1988.JPG 2x" data-file-width="909" data-file-height="727" /></a><figcaption>MC Lyte in 1988 at Firehouse Studios in Brooklyn with her producers Gizmo, Milk D and King of Chill and engineer Yoram Vazan.</figcaption></figure><p>In April 1988<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> she would release her debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Lyte_as_a_Rock" title="Lyte as a Rock">Lyte as a Rock</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-clip_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clip-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In addition to "I Cram to Understand U (Sam)" were released as singles "<a href="/wiki/Paper_Thin_(MC_Lyte_song)" title="Paper Thin (MC Lyte song)">Paper Thin</a>", the eponymous "<a href="/wiki/Lyte_as_a_Rock_(song)" title="Lyte as a Rock (song)">Lyte as a Rock</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/10%25_Dis" title="10% Dis">10% Dis</a>" (a <a href="/wiki/Diss_(music)" title="Diss (music)">diss track</a> to then-<a href="/wiki/Hurby_Azor" title="Hurby Azor">Hurby Azor</a> associate <a href="/wiki/Antoinette_(rapper)" title="Antoinette (rapper)">Antoinette</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-clip_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clip-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The album peaked #50 on the then <a href="/wiki/Top_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums"><i>Billboard</i> Top Black Albums</a>. Despite not having a great commercial performance, it is considered one of the best and most important rap albums, both in the 80s and in history.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> That year <a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a> magazine would rate Lyte as "the best female vocalist in hip-hop".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Lyte was also featured in the remix and music video of "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_Your_(Hands_on_Me)" title="I Want Your (Hands on Me)">I Want Your (Hands on Me)</a>" by Irish singer <a href="/wiki/Sin%C3%A9ad_O%27Connor" title="Sinéad O&#39;Connor">Sinéad O'Connor</a>, which debuted in May of that year on <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>.
</p><p>In January 1989 Lyte joined <a href="/wiki/Stop_the_Violence_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Stop the Violence Movement">Stop the Violence Movement</a> with <a href="/wiki/Boogie_Down_Productions" title="Boogie Down Productions">Boogie Down Productions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_Enemy_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Enemy (band)">Public Enemy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heavy_D" title="Heavy D">Heavy D</a>, among others. Together they released the single "Self Destruction" in response to violence in the hip hop and African American communities. The song debuted at #1 on the first week of <a href="/wiki/Hot_Rap_Songs" title="Hot Rap Songs"><i>Billboard</i> Hot Rap Singles</a> existence<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> and the proceeds were donated to the <a href="/wiki/National_Urban_League" title="National Urban League">National Urban League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Okayplayer_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Okayplayer-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In late August of that year, her song "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Not_Havin%27_It" title="I&#39;m Not Havin&#39; It">I'm Not Havin' It</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Positive_K" title="Positive K">Positive K</a> would have an entry on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot Rap Singles (peaking at #16), becoming MC Lyte's first appearance on a chart as solo artist. In October 1989 Lyte would publish her second album <i><a href="/wiki/Eyes_on_This" title="Eyes on This">Eyes on This</a></i>. This album, like its predecessor, received a great critical reception and is recognized as a hip hop classic.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> With <i>Eyes on This</i> she became the first solo female rapper to have an entry on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>. From this album came the singles "<a href="/wiki/Cha_Cha_Cha_(MC_Lyte_song)" title="Cha Cha Cha (MC Lyte song)">Cha Cha Cha</a>" (with which for the first time as solo artist she charted on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Songs" title="Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs"><i>Billboard</i> Hot Black Singles</a> and reached #1 on the Hot Rap Singles). "<a href="/wiki/Stop,_Look,_Listen_(MC_Lyte_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stop, Look, Listen (MC Lyte song)">Stop, Look, Listen</a>", and the <a href="/wiki/Political_hip_hop#Conscious_hip_hop" title="Political hip hop">socially conscious</a> "<a href="/wiki/Cappucino_(song)" title="Cappucino (song)">Cappucino</a>". During that year she also collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Foster_%26_McElroy" title="Foster &amp; McElroy">Foster &amp; McElroy</a>, known for their work with <a href="/wiki/En_Vogue" title="En Vogue">En Vogue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony!_Toni!_Ton%C3%A9!" title="Tony! Toni! Toné!">Tony! Toni! Toné!</a>, in the song "Dr. Soul". This single peaked #10 on <i>Billboard</i> Black Songs.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1990 MC Lyte performed at <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Hall" title="Carnegie Hall">Carnegie Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>MC Lyte's DJ since the start of her career, DJ K-Rock, is a cousin, Kennith Moorer; aside from a break in 1992, the two have toured consistently to the present.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> During that time she also had her own dancers, Leg One and Leg Two, who performed with her both in shows and in music videos.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1991.E2.80.931995:_Act_Like_You_Know_and_Ain.27t_No_Other"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1991–1995:_Act_Like_You_Know_and_Ain't_No_Other">1991–1995: <i>Act Like You Know</i> and <i>Ain't No Other</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1991–1995: Act Like You Know and Ain&#039;t No Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On May 1, 1991, Lyte performed on "Yo! Unplugged Rap", the first <a href="/wiki/MTV_Unplugged" title="MTV Unplugged">MTV Unplugged</a> to feature rap artists, alongside <a href="/wiki/A_Tribe_Called_Quest" title="A Tribe Called Quest">A Tribe Called Quest</a>, <a href="/wiki/De_La_Soul" title="De La Soul">De La Soul</a> and <a href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J" title="LL Cool J">LL Cool J</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Her performance was praised by <a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ken_Tucker" title="Ken Tucker">Ken Tucker</a>, who commented, "MC Lyte performed her song 'Cappucino' like a rapping <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">Aretha Franklin</a>: Lyte brought out the soul in her lyrics."<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In September 1991, Lyte released her third album, <i><a href="/wiki/Act_Like_You_Know_(MC_Lyte_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Act Like You Know (MC Lyte album)">Act Like You Know</a></i>, which incorporates a softer <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>/<a href="/wiki/New_Jack_Swing" class="mw-redirect" title="New Jack Swing">New Jack Swing</a> sound across some of the tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> This release received more mixed reviews than her previous albums and commercially it performed more weakly than its predecessor,  <i>Eyes on This</i>. From this album came the singles "<a href="/wiki/When_in_Love" title="When in Love">When in Love</a>" and the socially conscious "<a href="/wiki/Poor_Georgie" title="Poor Georgie">Poor Georgie</a>" (Lyte’s first entry on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> and her third #1 on the Hot Rap Singles) and "<a href="/wiki/Eyes_Are_the_Soul" title="Eyes Are the Soul">Eyes Are the Soul</a>".
That year she also participated in the socially conscious single "Heal Yourself" by the collective "HEAL Human Education Against Lies", which also included <a href="/wiki/Big_Daddy_Kane" title="Big Daddy Kane">Big Daddy Kane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boogie_Down_Productions" title="Boogie Down Productions">Boogie Down Productions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Run-DMC" title="Run-DMC">Run-DMC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen_Latifah" title="Queen Latifah">Queen Latifah</a> and LL Cool J.
</p><p>Between 1991 and 1992 Lyte participated in the  <i>"The Greatest Rap Show Ever"</i> concert held at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> with Public Enemy, <a href="/wiki/Naughty_by_Nature" title="Naughty by Nature">Naughty by Nature</a>, Queen Latifah, <a href="/wiki/Geto_Boys" title="Geto Boys">Geto Boys</a> and <a href="/wiki/DJ_Jazzy_Jeff_%26_The_Fresh_Prince" class="mw-redirect" title="DJ Jazzy Jeff &amp; The Fresh Prince">DJ Jazzy Jeff &amp; The Fresh Prince</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In the fall of 1991, she also performed in the hip-hop special <i><a href="/wiki/Dee_Barnes" title="Dee Barnes">Sisters In The Name of Rap</a></i> alongside <a href="/wiki/Salt-N-Pepa" title="Salt-N-Pepa">Salt-N-Pepa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yo-Yo_(rapper)" title="Yo-Yo (rapper)">Yo-Yo</a>, Queen Latifah and <a href="/wiki/Roxanne_Shant%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Roxanne Shanté">Roxanne Shanté</a>, among many others. it was recorded at the Ritz in NYC as a <a href="/wiki/Pay-per-view" title="Pay-per-view">pay-per-view</a> TV concert and released on <a href="/wiki/VHS" title="VHS">VHS</a> the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 1992, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Mo%27_Money_(soundtrack)" title="Mo&#39; Money (soundtrack)">Mo Money soundtrack</a>, MC Lyte collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Jam_and_Terry_Lewis" title="Jimmy Jam and Terry Lewis">Jimmy Jam and Terry Lewis</a>, known primarily for their work with <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a>, on the single "<a href="/wiki/Ice_Cream_Dream" title="Ice Cream Dream">Ice Cream Dream</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In 1992 she also performed on <a href="/wiki/Kris_Kross" title="Kris Kross">Kris Kross</a>'s <i>Back to School Jam</i> tour, which also featured A Tribe Called Quest and <a href="/wiki/Fu-Schnickens" title="Fu-Schnickens">Fu-Schnickens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Also during that year Lyte began work on her next album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Ain%27t_No_Other" title="Ain&#39;t No Other">Ain't No Other</a></i>, which was released on June 22, 1993. With this album, in which she adopts a more <a href="/wiki/Hardcore_hip_hop" title="Hardcore hip hop">hardcore</a> hip hop sound, Lyte achieved better critical reception than her predecessor. "<a href="/wiki/Ruffneck_(song)" title="Ruffneck (song)">Ruffneck</a>" was released as a single,<sup id="cite_ref-clip_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clip-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> which would become her first top 40 single on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, peaking at #35, and fourth #1 on the Hot Rap Singles, also earning her first <a href="/wiki/Gold_certification" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold certification">gold certification</a>. With "Ruffneck" MC Lyte would also get a nomination for the <a href="/wiki/36th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="36th Annual Grammy Awards">36th edition</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Best_Rap_Solo_Performance" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Rap Solo Performance">Best Rap Solo Performance</a> category. In October of that year, Lyte performed at the <i>1993 Budweiser Superfest</i> with <a href="/wiki/SWV" title="SWV">SWV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bell_Biv_Devoe" class="mw-redirect" title="Bell Biv Devoe">Bell Biv Devoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/LeVert" title="LeVert">LeVert</a>, Big Daddy Kane and <a href="/wiki/Silk_(group)" title="Silk (group)">Silk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 1994 MC Lyte participated on the performance on the finale of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Arsenio_Hall_Show" title="The Arsenio Hall Show">The Arsenio Hall Show</a></i>, alongside the likes of <a href="/wiki/KRS-One" title="KRS-One">KRS-One</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wu-Tang_Clan" title="Wu-Tang Clan">Wu-Tang Clan</a>, Naughty by Nature, <a href="/wiki/Guru_(rapper)" title="Guru (rapper)">Guru</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gang_Starr" title="Gang Starr">Gang Starr</a>, Yo-Yo, <a href="/wiki/Das_EFX" title="Das EFX">Das EFX</a> and A Tribe Called Quest, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In June collaborates with <a href="/wiki/Ice_Cube" title="Ice Cube">Ice Cube</a>, Public Enemy's <a href="/wiki/Chuck_D" title="Chuck D">Chuck D</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ice-T" title="Ice-T">Ice-T</a> on Public Enemy's <a href="/wiki/Terminator_X" title="Terminator X">Terminator X</a> album <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Bad_(Terminator_X_album)" title="Super Bad (Terminator X album)">Super Bad</a></i>. In the middle of 1994 she collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a> on the single remix and music video for "<a href="/wiki/You_Want_This" title="You Want This">You Want This</a>", peaking at #8 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 and earning a nomination for Music Video of the Year at the 2th edition of the <a href="/wiki/Soul_Train_Lady_of_Soul_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Soul Train Lady of Soul Awards">Soul Train Lady of Soul Awards</a>. Also during the summer of '94 participated in Janet Jackson's <a href="/wiki/Janet_World_Tour" title="Janet World Tour">Janet World Tour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early 1995, she collaborated with Queen Latifah and Yo-Yo on the remix of <a href="/wiki/Brandy_Norwood" title="Brandy Norwood">Brandy</a>'s top 10 single "<a href="/wiki/I_Wanna_Be_Down" title="I Wanna Be Down">I Wanna Be Down</a>", earning a nomination at the <a href="/wiki/1995_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="1995 MTV Video Music Awards">12th edition</a> of the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Video Music Award">MTV Video Music Award</a> in the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Rap_Video" title="MTV Video Music Award for Best Rap Video">Best Rap Video</a> category. In April of that year collaborated alongside <a href="/wiki/Meshell_Ndegeocello" title="Meshell Ndegeocello">Meshell Ndegeocello</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patra_(singer)" title="Patra (singer)">Patra</a>, Yo-Yo, Latifah, <a href="/wiki/Salt-N-Pepa" title="Salt-N-Pepa">Salt-N-Pepa</a> and <a href="/wiki/TLC_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="TLC (band)">TLC</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Lopes" title="Lisa Lopes"><i> Left Eye </i> Lopes</a> in the rap remix of "<a href="/wiki/Freedom_(Theme_from_Panther)" title="Freedom (Theme from Panther)">Freedom</a>" on the <i><a href="/wiki/Panther_(film)" title="Panther (film)">Panther</a></i> movie <a href="/wiki/Panther_(film)#soundtrack" title="Panther (film)">soundtrack</a><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>  In June she performed at the <i>Jam for Peace</i> with <a href="/wiki/Warren_G" title="Warren G">Warren G</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brownstone_(group)" title="Brownstone (group)">Brownstone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adina_Howard" title="Adina Howard">Adina Howard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montell_Jordan" title="Montell Jordan">Montell Jordan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soul_for_Real" title="Soul for Real">Soul for Real</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> That year she also collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Lin_Que" title="Lin Que">Lin Que</a> on the remix of Mary J. Blige's "<a href="/wiki/You_Bring_Me_Joy_(Mary_J._Blige_song)" title="You Bring Me Joy (Mary J. Blige song)">You Bring Me Joy</a>".
</p>
<h3><span id="1996.E2.80.931998:_Bad_as_I_Wanna_B_and_Seven_.26_Seven"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1996–1998:_Bad_as_I_Wanna_B_and_Seven_&amp;_Seven">1996–1998: <i>Bad as I Wanna B</i> and <i>Seven &amp; Seven</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1996–1998: Bad as I Wanna B and Seven &amp; Seven">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:M.C._Lyte_1996.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/M.C._Lyte_1996.jpg/220px-M.C._Lyte_1996.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="254" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/M.C._Lyte_1996.jpg/330px-M.C._Lyte_1996.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/M.C._Lyte_1996.jpg/440px-M.C._Lyte_1996.jpg 2x" data-file-width="997" data-file-height="1149" /></a><figcaption>MC Lyte in 1996</figcaption></figure><p> In February 1996, MC Lyte collaborated on the R&amp;B group <a href="/wiki/Xscape_(group)" title="Xscape (group)">Xscape</a>'s single "<a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Hang/Do_You_Want_To" class="mw-redirect" title="Can&#39;t Hang/Do You Want To">Can't Hang</a>". In that month also collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Lord_Finesse" title="Lord Finesse">Lord Finesse</a> on the interlude "Taking It Lyte" from his album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Awakening_(Lord_Finesse_album)" title="The Awakening (Lord Finesse album)">The Awakening</a></i>. In March, after signing with <a href="/wiki/East_West_Records" title="East West Records">East West Records</a>, she released "<a href="/wiki/Keep_On_Keepin%27_On_(MC_Lyte_song)" title="Keep On Keepin&#39; On (MC Lyte song)">Keep On Keepin' On</a>", the first single from her forthcoming album. This new collaboration with Xscape reached #10 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, her highest position on this chart as main artist, getting a gold certification. "Keep On Keepin' On" would also be part of the <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Park_(soundtrack)" title="Sunset Park (soundtrack)">soundtrack</a> of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Sunset_Park_(film)" title="Sunset Park (film)">Sunset Park</a></i>. In September win the Best R&amp;B, Soul or Rap Video category in the 3th edition of <a href="/wiki/Soul_Train_Lady_of_Soul_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Soul Train Lady of Soul Awards">Soul Train Lady of Soul Awards</a> with this song.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In August of that same year, Lyte released her fifth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Bad_as_I_Wanna_B" title="Bad as I Wanna B">Bad as I Wanna B</a></i>. With tracks with a <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">Pop</a>/R&amp;B-oriented sound<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> the album would receive mixed reviews. In November, is released as single a <a href="/wiki/Sean_%22Puffy%22_Combs" class="mw-redirect" title="Sean &quot;Puffy&quot; Combs">Sean "Puffy" Combs</a> remix of "<a href="/wiki/Cold_Rock_a_Party" title="Cold Rock a Party">Cold Rock a Party</a>" featuring <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-clip_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clip-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> This single peaked at #11 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 and would become her fifth #1 single on the Hot Rap Singles (fourth as lead artist), earning a gold certification. It also enters the top 40 of various charts outside the United States, being #1 and certified <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_certification" title="Music recording certification">platinum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Recorded_Music_NZ" title="Recorded Music NZ">New Zealand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 1997 "Keep on Pushin" was included in the <a href="/wiki/Dangerous_Ground_(soundtrack)" title="Dangerous Ground (soundtrack)">soundtrack</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Dangerous_Ground_(1997_film)" title="Dangerous Ground (1997 film)">Dangerous Ground</a></i>, in which MC Lyte, <a href="/wiki/Bahamadia" title="Bahamadia">Bahamadia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nonchalant" title="Nonchalant">Nonchalant</a> and Yo-Yo collaborate under the production of <a href="/wiki/Pete_Rock" title="Pete Rock">Pete Rock</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In March 1997, she collaborated with <a href="/wiki/R%26B" class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Billy_Lawrence" title="Billy Lawrence">Billy Lawrence</a> on the single "<a href="/wiki/Come_On_(Billy_Lawrence_song)" title="Come On (Billy Lawrence song)">Come On</a>", which was included in the soundtrack of the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Set_It_Off_(film)#Music" title="Set It Off (film)">Set it Off</a></i>. Between June and July of that year she embarked on a <a href="/wiki/United_Service_Organizations" title="United Service Organizations">USO</a> Tour, performing for American troops in Italy and Greece.<sup id="cite_ref-Hess_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hess-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In November she collaborated with LL Cool J and <a href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes" title="Busta Rhymes">Busta Rhymes</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Levert.Sweat.Gill" title="Levert.Sweat.Gill">debut album</a> of the R&amp;B <a href="/wiki/Supergroup_(music)" title="Supergroup (music)">supergroup</a> <a href="/wiki/LSG_(band)" title="LSG (band)">LSG</a> on the track "Curious", which was later released as single. That year Lyte also collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Parliament-Funkadelic" title="Parliament-Funkadelic">Parliament-Funkadelic</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Bootsy_Collins" title="Bootsy Collins">Bootsy Collins</a> on the single "I'm Leavin U (Gotta Go, Gotta Go)" from his album <i><a href="/wiki/Fresh_Outta_%27P%27_University" title="Fresh Outta &#39;P&#39; University">Fresh Outta 'P' University</a></i>.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mc_lyte-05.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Mc_lyte-05.jpg/220px-Mc_lyte-05.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="331" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Mc_lyte-05.jpg/330px-Mc_lyte-05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Mc_lyte-05.jpg/440px-Mc_lyte-05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="899" data-file-height="1353" /></a><figcaption>MC Lyte in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> in 1998</figcaption></figure>
<p>In August 1998 MC Lyte released her sixth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Seven_%26_Seven_(MC_Lyte_album)" title="Seven &amp; Seven (MC Lyte album)">Seven &amp; Seven</a></i>. This would have a poor commercial and critical reception despite having the collaboration of famous producers and artists such as <a href="/wiki/The_Neptunes" title="The Neptunes">The Neptunes</a>, LL Cool J, Missy Elliott, <a href="/wiki/L.E.S._(record_producer)" title="L.E.S. (record producer)">L.E.S.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trackmasters" title="Trackmasters">Trackmasters</a>, which would lead to Lyte's departure from EastWest Records. That year she also embarks again on a USO Tour, performing in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-Hess_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hess-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1999.E2.80.932012:_Collaborations_and_releases_independently"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1999–2012:_Collaborations_and_releases_independently">1999–2012: Collaborations and releases independently</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1999–2012: Collaborations and releases independently">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In November 1999 MC Lyte collaborated in the remix of <a href="/wiki/Jamming_(song)" title="Jamming (song)">Jammin</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bob_Marley" title="Bob Marley">Bob Marley</a> in the remix album <i><a href="/wiki/Chant_Down_Babylon" title="Chant Down Babylon">Chant Down Babylon</a></i>. This track would later be released as single. During that month she also collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Will_Smith" title="Will Smith">Will Smith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tatyana_Ali" title="Tatyana Ali">Tatyana Ali</a> on "Who Am I" from Smith's album <i><a href="/wiki/Willennium" title="Willennium">Willennium</a></i>.
</p><p>In March 2000 MC Lyte collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Common_(rapper)" title="Common (rapper)">Common</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bilal_(American_singer)" title="Bilal (American singer)">Bilal</a> on the track "A Film Called (Pimp)" on Common's album <i><a href="/wiki/Like_Water_for_Chocolate_(album)" title="Like Water for Chocolate (album)">Like Water for Chocolate</a></i>.
</p><p>In September 2001 her first compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Very_Best_of_MC_Lyte" title="The Very Best of MC Lyte">The Very Best of MC Lyte</a></i> was released.
</p><p>In April 2002 the soundtrack for the TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Angel_(American_TV_series)" title="Dark Angel (American TV series)">Dark Angel</a></i> is released, which includes Lyte's songs "Dark Angel Theme" (in collaboration with Public Enemy) and "No Dealz" (with Ericka Yancey). In May of that year, MC Lyte collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Angie_Stone" title="Angie Stone">Angie Stone</a> on the album version of "<a href="/wiki/Jam_for_the_Ladies" title="Jam for the Ladies">Jam for the Ladies</a>" by electronica musician <a href="/wiki/Moby" title="Moby">Moby</a>. In November she collaborates with <a href="/wiki/Erick_Sermon" title="Erick Sermon">Erick Sermon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rah_Digga" title="Rah Digga">Rah Digga</a> on the track "Tell Me" on Sermon's album <i><a href="/wiki/React_(Erick_Sermon_album)" title="React (Erick Sermon album)">React</a></i>. During that time Lyte also became honorary member of Sermon and <a href="/wiki/Redman_(rapper)" title="Redman (rapper)">Redman</a>'s supergroup <a href="/wiki/Def_Squad" title="Def Squad">Def Squad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hdd_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdd-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2003, Lyte released the independently produced record <i><a href="/wiki/Da_Undaground_Heat,_Vol._1" title="Da Undaground Heat, Vol. 1">Da Undaground Heat, Vol. 1</a></i>, featuring <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Foxx" title="Jamie Foxx">Jamie Foxx</a>. The album has little commercial impact and mixed reviews, but the single "<a href="/wiki/Ride_Wit_Me" class="mw-redirect" title="Ride Wit Me">Ride Wit Me</a>" get a nomination for the <a href="/wiki/46th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="46th Annual Grammy Awards">46th edition</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Rap_Solo_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Rap Solo Performance">Best Female Rap Vocal Performance</a> category. In June of that year she teamed the rock group <a href="/wiki/Aerosmith" title="Aerosmith">Aerosmith</a>, Public Enemy's <a href="/wiki/Chuck_D" title="Chuck D">Chuck D</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flavor_Flav" title="Flavor Flav">Flavor Flav</a>, Busta Rhymes and <a href="/wiki/Phife_Dawg" title="Phife Dawg">Phife Dawg</a> in the group the Spitballers. Together release "Let's Get Loud (Everybody Get Up)", which became the opening song of the 11th edition of the  <a href="/wiki/ESPY_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="ESPY Awards">ESPY Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In August Lyte collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>, Missy Elliott and <a href="/wiki/Free_Marie" title="Free Marie">Free</a> on the single "<a href="/wiki/Fighting_Temptation" title="Fighting Temptation">Fighting Temptation</a>" as part of the soundtrack for <a href="/wiki/The_Fighting_Temptations" title="The Fighting Temptations">the homonymous film</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> That same month she released the compilation album <i>The Shit I Never Dropped</i>, which includes previously unreleased collaborations with En Vogue's <a href="/wiki/Dawn_Robinson" title="Dawn Robinson">Dawn Robinson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Da_Brat" title="Da Brat">Da Brat</a>, Missy Elliott, Erick Sermon and <a href="/wiki/Clipse" title="Clipse">Clipse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In September collaborates with <a href="/wiki/Black_Eyed_Peas" title="Black Eyed Peas">Black Eyed Peas</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fergie_(singer)" title="Fergie (singer)">Fergie</a> on the track "Mash Out" on will.i.am album <i><a href="/wiki/Must_B_21" title="Must B 21">Must B 21</a></i>.
</p><p>In May 2004, MC Lyte collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Teena_Marie" title="Teena Marie">Teena Marie</a> and Medusa on the song "The Mackin' Game" from Teena Marie's album <i><a href="/wiki/La_Do%C3%B1a_(album)" title="La Doña (album)">La Doña</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In August he collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Boyz_II_Men" title="Boyz II Men">Boyz II Men</a> on their cover of "<a href="/wiki/What_You_Won%27t_Do_for_Love_(song)" title="What You Won&#39;t Do for Love (song)">What You Won't Do for Love</a>". That year Lyte was also nominated at the <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards_2004" title="BET Awards 2004">4th edition</a> of the <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards" title="BET Awards">BET Awards</a> in the <a href="/wiki/BET_Award_for_Best_Female_Hip_Hop_Artist" title="BET Award for Best Female Hip Hop Artist">Best Female Hip Hop Artist</a> category.
</p><p>In 2005, she released two songs produced by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wolf" title="Richard Wolf">Richard "Wolfie" Wolf</a> called "Can I Get It Now" and "Don't Walk Away". MC Lyte's song "My Main Aim" was the title song of the basketball video game <i><a href="/wiki/NBA_Live_2005" title="NBA Live 2005">NBA Live 2005</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/EA_Sports" title="EA Sports">EA Sports</a>. That year also collaborated with the Polish-born German producer <a href="/wiki/DJ_Tomekk" title="DJ Tomekk">DJ Tomekk</a> on the track "Partyverlauf" from his album <i><a href="/wiki/Numma_Eyns" title="Numma Eyns">Numma Eyns</a></i>.
</p><p>In July 2006 MC Lyte releases "The Wonder Years" in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/DJ_Premier" title="DJ Premier">DJ Premier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In October of that year, Lyte was one of the artists honored at the 3th edition of the <a href="/wiki/Hip_Hop_Honors" title="Hip Hop Honors">VH1 Hip Hop Honors</a>, where she perform with Da Brat, <a href="/wiki/Lil%27_Kim" title="Lil&#39; Kim">Lil' Kim</a>, Yo-Yo and <a href="/wiki/Remy_Ma" title="Remy Ma">Remy Ma</a>. Lyte would be the first female solo rapper to achieve this recognition.<sup id="cite_ref-HHH_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HHH-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> During that time also performed on the <i>"Ebony Black Family Reunion Tour"</i> along with <a href="/wiki/Doug_E._Fresh" title="Doug E. Fresh">Doug E. Fresh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slick_Rick" title="Slick Rick">Slick Rick</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Whodini" title="Whodini">Whodini</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:MC_Lyte.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/MC_Lyte.jpg/220px-MC_Lyte.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="331" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5b/MC_Lyte.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="451" /></a><figcaption>Lyte at the October 14, 2007 <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a></figcaption></figure><p> In 2007 MC Lyte joined <a href="/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">The Roots</a> and Big Daddy Kane on the <i>"VH1 Hip Hop Honors Tour"</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> On July 9 performed at the opening of the 25th annual <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Jr._Concert_Series" title="Martin Luther King Jr. Concert Series">Martin Luther King Jr. Concert Series</a> in Brooklyn. That month also performed for first time at the <i><a href="/wiki/Essence_Music_Festival" title="Essence Music Festival">Essence Music Festival</a></i> in New Orleans.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In 2007 Lyte also released the singles "Mad At Me" and "Money" with KRS-One, the latter part of KRS-One's album <i><a href="/wiki/Adventures_in_Emceein" title="Adventures in Emceein">Adventures in Emceein</a></i>.
</p><p>In May 2008, as member of the group Almost September with Philip "Whitey" White and <a href="/wiki/Jared_Lee_Gosselin" title="Jared Lee Gosselin">Jared Lee Gosselin</a>, MC Lyte released <i><a href="/wiki/The_Almost_September_EP" class="mw-redirect" title="The Almost September EP">The Almost September EP</a></i>. This features an <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>/<a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">Soul</a> oriented sound.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Later she embarks with the group on a tour in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> In June is released the song "Closer", a collaboration with her cousin <a href="/wiki/Charles_Hamilton_(rapper)" title="Charles Hamilton (rapper)">Charles Hamilton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> In October of that year performed "Cha Cha Cha" at the <a href="/wiki/2008_BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="2008 BET Hip Hop Awards">3th edition</a> of the <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In December MC Lyte collaborates with <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> on "BK Anthem".<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2009 Lyte collaborated with <a href="/wiki/India_Arie" title="India Arie">India Arie</a> on the track "Psalms 23" from her album <i><a href="/wiki/Testimony:_Vol._2,_Love_%26_Politics" title="Testimony: Vol. 2, Love &amp; Politics">Testimony: Vol. 2, Love &amp; Politics</a></i>. In June of that year, Lyte collaborated again with Teena Marie on the track "The Pressure" from her latest album <i><a href="/wiki/Congo_Square_(album)" title="Congo Square (album)">Congo Square</a></i>. In that year also released the single with a <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">Reggae</a>-oriented sound "Brooklyn".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2010, she performed on the concert/TV Special <i><a href="/wiki/VH1_Divas#VH1_Divas_Salute_The_Troops" title="VH1 Divas">VH1 Divas Salute The Troops</a></i>, which also featured <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keri_Hilson" title="Keri Hilson">Keri Hilson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Heart_(band)" title="Heart (band)">Heart</a>.
</p><p>In 2011 MC Lyte performed again at the <i>Essence Music Festival</i><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> and released the single "Dada da Da".
</p><p>In March 2012 collaborated with Grammy-winning singer <a href="/wiki/Macy_Gray" title="Macy Gray">Macy Gray</a> on the interlude "Really (Skit)" from her album <i><a href="/wiki/Covered_(Macy_Gray_album)" title="Covered (Macy Gray album)">Covered</a></i>. That year she also released the single "Dopestyle" and her own <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">Mobile app</a> <i>MC Lyte App</i>, where publishes her exclusive musical releases.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2013.E2.80.93present:_Legend_and_following_projects"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–present:_Legend_and_following_projects">2013–present: <i>Legend</i> and following projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2013–present: Legend and following projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2013 MC Lyte receives the Lifetime Achievement Award at <a href="/wiki/Russell_Simmons" title="Russell Simmons">Russell Simmons</a>'s Hip Hop Inaugural Ball.<sup id="cite_ref-ib_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ib-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In June of that year releases "Cravin'" in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/High_School_Musical:_Get_in_the_Picture" title="High School Musical: Get in the Picture">Stan Carrizosa</a> as the first single from her forthcoming album.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In October, Lyte was honored with the Icon Lifetime Achievement "I Am Hip Hop" at the <a href="/wiki/2013_BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="2013 BET Hip Hop Awards">8th edition</a> of the <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a> for her contributions to hip-hop culture.<sup id="cite_ref-BETHH_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BETHH-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2014, "<a href="/wiki/Dear_John_(MC_Lyte_song)" title="Dear John (MC Lyte song)">Dear John</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Common_(rapper)" title="Common (rapper)">Common</a> &amp; 10Beats) was released as the second single.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> That same month she reunited with Queen Latifah, Brandy and Yo-Yo to perform "I Wanna Be Down" at the <a href="/wiki/2014_BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="2014 BET Hip Hop Awards">2014 BET Hip Hop Awards</a> in celebration of its 20th anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> On October 14, 2014, MC Lyte performed "Cha Cha Cha" and "Dear John" to the President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> at the celebration of the 50th anniversary of the legislation that created the <a href="/wiki/National_Endowment_for_the_Humanities" title="National Endowment for the Humanities">National Endowment for the Humanities</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Endowment_for_the_Arts" title="National Endowment for the Arts">National Endowment for the Arts</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> becoming the first female artist to perform Hip Hop at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In November released "Ball" as the third single.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2015, MC Lyte released <i><a href="/wiki/Legend_(MC_Lyte_album)" title="Legend (MC Lyte album)">Legend</a></i>, her eighth solo album and her first full-length studio album in 12 years.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> As part of <i><a href="/wiki/Record_Store_Day" title="Record Store Day">Record Store Day</a></i>, the album was available for 24 hours only on a limited-edition <a href="/wiki/Phonograph_record" title="Phonograph record">vinyl</a> collector's item.<sup id="cite_ref-complex_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Shortly before the album's release, the fourth and final single "Check" was released.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2016 Lyte performs at the <i>Essence Music Festival</i> in New Orleans.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> In September she is awarded the <a href="/wiki/W._E._B._Du_Bois_Medal" class="mw-redirect" title="W. E. B. Du Bois Medal">W. E. B. Du Bois Medal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>'s highest honor in the field of African and African-American studies.<sup id="cite_ref-hu_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hu-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In October collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Eric_Ben%C3%A9t" title="Eric Benét">Eric Benét</a> on the track "Holdin' On" from <a href="/wiki/Eric_Ben%C3%A9t_(album)" title="Eric Benét (album)">his eponymous album</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 11, 2017, during <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">Hot 97</a>'s annual <a href="/wiki/Summer_Jam_(festival)" title="Summer Jam (festival)">Summer Jam</a> music festival, Remy Ma brought out MC Lyte, along with <a href="/wiki/The_Lady_of_Rage" title="The Lady of Rage">The Lady of Rage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardi_B" title="Cardi B">Cardi B</a>, <a href="/wiki/Young_M.A" title="Young M.A">Young M.A</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monie_Love" title="Monie Love">Monie Love</a>, Lil' Kim, and Queen Latifah, to celebrate female rappers and perform Latifah's 1993 hit single "<a href="/wiki/U.N.I.T.Y." title="U.N.I.T.Y.">U.N.I.T.Y.</a>" about <a href="/wiki/Female_empowerment" class="mw-redirect" title="Female empowerment">female empowerment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Also released the single "Money on My Mind."
</p><p>During 2018, she continued to release a strand of singles, one of which was 'Easy', in response to her British audience claiming that artists who recorded <a href="/wiki/New_jack_swing" title="New jack swing">new jack swing</a> were sexually explicit. In July of that year she was special guest on Queen Latifah's show "Ladies First" on <i>Essence Music Festival</i> along with Brandy, Missy Elliott, Salt-N-Pepa, Roxanne Shante, Yo-Yo, Monie Love and Remy Ma.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2019 received The Trail Blazer Award at the Trumpet Awards in Atlanta with Yo Yo, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Mama" title="Lil Mama">Lil Mama</a>, Da Brat, <a href="/wiki/Big_Tigger" title="Big Tigger">Big Tigger</a>, and DJ K-Rock helping to celebrate with a performance of Lyte songs.<sup id="cite_ref-ta_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ta-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Other ventures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting">Acting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Acting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Her first acting role was in 1991, an off-Broadway theater play titled <i>Club Twelve</i>, a hip-hop twist on <i><a href="/wiki/Twelfth_Night" title="Twelfth Night">Twelfth Night</a></i> alongside <a href="/wiki/Wyclef_Jean" title="Wyclef Jean">Wyclef Jean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">Lauryn Hill</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Nicole_Carson" title="Lisa Nicole Carson">Lisa Nicole Carson</a>. After she made her film debut in the 1993 movie titled <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fly_by_Night_(1993_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fly by Night (1993 film) (page does not exist)">Fly by Night</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fly_by_Night_(film,_1993)" class="extiw" title="fr:Fly by Night (film, 1993)">fr</a>&#93;</span></i>, starring alongside <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Sams" class="mw-redirect" title="Jeffrey Sams">Jeffrey Sams</a>, Ron Brice, and Steve Gomer, she also starred other films, such as <i>A Luv Tale</i> (1999), <i><a href="/wiki/Train_Ride" title="Train Ride">Train Ride</a></i> (2000), <i><a href="/wiki/Civil_Brand" title="Civil Brand">Civil Brand</a></i> (2002) and <i>Playa's Ball</i> (2003). In 2011, she guest starred in the <i><a href="/wiki/Regular_Show" title="Regular Show">Regular Show</a></i> episode "Rap It Up", portraying a member of a hip-hop group also including characters voiced by <a href="/wiki/Tyler,_the_Creator" title="Tyler, the Creator">Tyler, the Creator</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donald_Glover" title="Donald Glover">Childish Gambino</a>. Lyte signed with the production unit, Duc Tha Moon, for three years and eventually made a deal with Sirius Satellite Radio. Lyte also made appearances on the following television shows: Lyric Cafe, Hip Hop Honors, and Black in the 80's.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In June 2006, MC Lyte was interviewed for the documentary <i>The Rap Report, Part 2</i>. MC Lyte talked about her career in rap music and what it was like during the beginnings of hip hop. She also performs a concert of her most famous hits. The program is produced by Rex Barnett.
</p><p>In 2007, Lyte joined the cast of MTV's <i>Celebrity Rap Superstar</i><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> and coached <a href="/wiki/Shar_Jackson" title="Shar Jackson">Shar Jackson</a> to a hip hop emcee victory in a mere eight weeks.
</p><p>In 2017 Lyte played Detective Makena Daniels in the drama series <a href="/wiki/Tales_(TV_series)" title="Tales (TV series)"><i>Tales</i></a>. Immediately following she played DEA Special Agent Katrina 'K.C.' Walsh in the Police drama <i><a href="/wiki/S.W.A.T._(2017_TV_series)" title="S.W.A.T. (2017 TV series)">S.W.A.T.</a></i> and Tiffany in <a href="/wiki/TV_One_(U.S._TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="TV One (U.S. TV network)">TV ONE</a> production <i>Loved to Death</i>. Lyte has been featured on television as herself on such shows as <i><a href="/wiki/In_Living_Color" title="In Living Color">In Living Color</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Moesha" title="Moesha">Moesha</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Cousin_Skeeter" title="Cousin Skeeter">Cousin Skeeter</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Undercover" title="New York Undercover">New York Undercover</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/My_Wife_and_Kids" title="My Wife and Kids">My Wife and Kids</a></i>, and <i>Sisters in the Name of Rap</i>. She also acted on such TV shows as <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_House_(TV_series)" title="In the House (TV series)">In the House</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Real_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Get Real (U.S. TV series)">Get Real</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Half_%26_Half" title="Half &amp; Half">Half &amp; Half</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_of_the_South_(TV_series)" title="Queen of the South (TV series)">Queen of the South</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_District" title="The District">The District</a></i>.
</p><p>In 2020, Lyte starred in <i><a href="/wiki/Bad_Hair_(2020_film)" title="Bad Hair (2020 film)">Bad Hair</a></i> directed by <a href="/wiki/Justin_Simien" title="Justin Simien">Justin Simien</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Sylvie%27s_Love" title="Sylvie&#39;s Love">Sylvie's Love</a></i>, a period piece set in the 1960s opposite <a href="/wiki/Tessa_Thompson" title="Tessa Thompson">Tessa Thompson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021 and 2022, Lyte starred as Tina Nixon in VH1's Hip Hop Family Christmas and its respective sequel, Hip Hop Family Christmas Wedding alongside <a href="/wiki/Keri_Hilson" title="Keri Hilson">Keri Hilson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ne-Yo" title="Ne-Yo">Ne-Yo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terrence_J" title="Terrence J">Terrence J</a>, <a href="/wiki/Redman_(rapper)" title="Redman (rapper)">Redman</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Serayah_(actress)" title="Serayah (actress)">Serayah</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_and_commerce">Business and commerce</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Business and commerce">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>MC Lyte opened Shaitel, a Los Angeles boutique that specialized in accessories from belts to sunglasses. "We sell a mixture of new and vintage [items]," she explained. "We also have a few signature pieces that are done just for the store. We boast to bring a little New York flavor out here to California."<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1997, MC Lyte launched Sunni Gyrl Inc., a global entertainment firm that specializes in artist management and development, production, and creative services and consulting.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voiceover">Voiceover</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Voiceover">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1996, MC Lyte began doing voiceovers, working on a short-lived BET show called <i>The Boot</i> and doing some branding for the Starz network, <a href="/wiki/Tide_(brand)" title="Tide (brand)">Tide</a>, <a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">AT&amp;T</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Urban_League" title="National Urban League">National Urban League</a>, and many others. She did the voice of Tia for the Mattel toy line <a href="/wiki/Diva_Starz" title="Diva Starz">Diva Starz</a> from 2000 to 2002.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="DJing">DJing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: DJing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>DJ MC Lyte served as the DJ of choice at <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jordan" title="Michael Jordan">Michael Jordan</a>'s 50th Birthday Celebration, at his 2013 wedding reception, and at <a href="/wiki/Jay_Leno" title="Jay Leno">Jay Leno</a>'s farewell party.  Lyte has gone on to provide music for The <a href="/wiki/Image_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Image Awards">Image Awards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan</a>, Google, <a href="/wiki/Black_Enterprise" title="Black Enterprise">Black Enterprise</a>, and many others.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Speaker">Speaker</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Speaker">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>MC Lyte has spoken at colleges and universities, for organizations around the globe, and with notable people like <a href="/wiki/Iyanla_Vanzant" title="Iyanla Vanzant">Iyanla Vanzant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russell_Simmons" title="Russell Simmons">Russell Simmons</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Soledad_O%27Brien" title="Soledad O&#39;Brien">Soledad O'Brien</a> bringing a message of empowerment from her book <i>Unstoppable: Igniting the Power Within to Achieve Your Greatest Potential</i>. She also partnered with the <a href="/wiki/Thurgood_Marshall_College_Fund" title="Thurgood Marshall College Fund">Thurgood Marshall College Fund</a> on the iLEAD international tour<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> in South Africa to empower the continent's youth and up-and-coming leaders.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership_and_philanthropy">Leadership and philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Leadership and philanthropy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1991, MC Lyte was featured in TV informercial promoting pro-choice abortion rights political action "The Most Exciting Women in Music" alongside <a href="/wiki/Corina_(American_singer)" title="Corina (American singer)">Corina</a>, Juliet Cuming, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Gordon" title="Kim Gordon">Kim Gordon</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sonic_Youth" title="Sonic Youth">Sonic Youth</a>), <a href="/wiki/Lady_Miss_Kier" title="Lady Miss Kier">Lady Miss Kier</a> (<a href="/wiki/Deee-Lite" title="Deee-Lite">Deee-Lite</a>), <a href="/wiki/Kate_Pierson" title="Kate Pierson">Kate Pierson</a> (<a href="/wiki/The_B-52%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="The B-52&#39;s">The B-52's</a>), <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Waters" title="Crystal Waters">Crystal Waters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tina_Weymouth" title="Tina Weymouth">Tina Weymouth</a> (<a href="/wiki/Talking_Heads" title="Talking Heads">Talking Heads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Tom_Club" title="Tom Tom Club">Tom Tom Club</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2006, her diary, as well as a <a href="/wiki/Phonograph" title="Phonograph">turntable</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gramophone_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Gramophone record">records</a>, and other assorted ephemera from the early days of hip hop, were donated to the <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">Smithsonian Institution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> This collection, entitled "Hip-Hop Won't Stop: The Beat, the Rhymes, the Life" is a program to assemble objects of historical relevance to the hip hop genre from its inception.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
MC Lyte served as the President of the Los Angeles Chapter of the Recording Academy (the <a href="/wiki/Grammy" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy">Grammy</a> organization) from 2011 to 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-explains_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-explains-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> She was the first African American woman to serve in this role.<sup id="cite_ref-explains_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-explains-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>She is the founder of Hip Hop Sisters Foundation,<sup id="cite_ref-Grimm_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grimm-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> which presented two $100,000 scholarships to college students each of the first two years of its inception and three $50,000 scholarships as a part of its #EducateOurMen initiative during its third year during the <a href="/wiki/Soul_Train_Music_Awards" title="Soul Train Music Awards">Soul Train Music Awards</a> Red Carpet Preshow.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Artistry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Influences.2C_style_and_rapping_technique"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences,_style_and_rapping_technique">Influences, style and rapping technique</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Influences, style and rapping technique">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>MC Lyte has considered artists such as <a href="/wiki/Salt-N-Pepa" title="Salt-N-Pepa">Salt-N-Pepa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rakim" title="Rakim">Rakim</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-xxli_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxli-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roxanne_Shant%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Roxanne Shanté">Roxanne Shanté</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Doug_E._Fresh" title="Doug E. Fresh">Doug E. Fresh</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kool_Moe_Dee" title="Kool Moe Dee">Kool Moe Dee</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-xxli_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxli-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sha-Rock" title="Sha-Rock">Sha-Rock</a> from <a href="/wiki/Funky_4_%2B_1" title="Funky 4 + 1">Funky 4 + 1</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Run-DMC" title="Run-DMC">Run-DMC</a><sup id="cite_ref-xxli_106-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxli-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> as her inspirations early in her musical career. In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL</a></i> in 2013, Lyte talks about the influence in her early days of <a href="/wiki/Melle_Mel" title="Melle Mel">Melle Mel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grandmaster_Flash_and_the_Furious_Five" title="Grandmaster Flash and the Furious Five">Grandmaster Flash and the Furious Five</a> (specifically the song "<a href="/wiki/The_Message_(Grandmaster_Flash_and_the_Furious_Five_song)" title="The Message (Grandmaster Flash and the Furious Five song)">The Message</a>"). She also claimed to know "all the words" on <a href="/wiki/Kurtis_Blow" title="Kurtis Blow">Kurtis Blow</a>'s records.<sup id="cite_ref-xxli_106-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxli-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Throughout her career, has also paid tribute to other artists such as <a href="/wiki/Spoonie_Gee" title="Spoonie Gee">Spoonie Gee</a> (who she covered on <i>Act Like You Know</i>), <a href="/wiki/Slick_Rick" title="Slick Rick">Slick Rick</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Rock_Steady_Crew" class="mw-redirect" title="The Rock Steady Crew">The Rock Steady Crew</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J" title="LL Cool J">LL Cool J</a><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Latifah" title="Queen Latifah">Queen Latifah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Source" title="The Source">The Source</a></i> in 2015, when asked about her motivation to record her latest album, <i><a href="/wiki/Legend_(MC_Lyte_album)" title="Legend (MC Lyte album)">Legend</a></i>, Lyte said she was inspired by <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a>, among other rappers.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Her style of rap has been described in the book <i>Listen to Rap! Exploring a Musical Genre</i> as "mid-tempo but aggressive (lots of plosives) and carefully articulated, with emphasis on end rhymes."<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Smithsonian_National_Museum_of_American_History_-_Crazy_Legs_Jacket_(3051395095).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Smithsonian_National_Museum_of_American_History_-_Crazy_Legs_Jacket_%283051395095%29.jpg/220px-Smithsonian_National_Museum_of_American_History_-_Crazy_Legs_Jacket_%283051395095%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Smithsonian_National_Museum_of_American_History_-_Crazy_Legs_Jacket_%283051395095%29.jpg/330px-Smithsonian_National_Museum_of_American_History_-_Crazy_Legs_Jacket_%283051395095%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Smithsonian_National_Museum_of_American_History_-_Crazy_Legs_Jacket_%283051395095%29.jpg/440px-Smithsonian_National_Museum_of_American_History_-_Crazy_Legs_Jacket_%283051395095%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption>MC Lyte's diary displayed in <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_American_History" title="National Museum of American History">National Museum of American History</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Greg Prato of <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a>, referred to her as one of the first female rappers to "point out the sexism and misogyny that often runs rampant in hip-hop", often taking the subject "head on lyrically" in her songs.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Times" title="Birmingham Times">The Birmingham Times</a></i> has credited her for helping transition hip-hop from the "feel-good, party vibe" of the late 1970s into a "socially conscious form of expression," as the rapper addressed issues like racism, sexism, and the drug culture had been affecting the African-American community.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a> have cited her as a "hip-hop pioneer".<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>MC Lyte has influenced the work of later female rappers such as <a href="/wiki/Queen_Latifah" title="Queen Latifah">Queen Latifah</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lil%27_Kim" title="Lil&#39; Kim">Lil' Kim</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Da_Brat" title="Da Brat">Da Brat</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">Lauryn Hill</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Monie_Love" title="Monie Love">Monie Love</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eve_(rapper)" title="Eve (rapper)">Eve</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rapsody" title="Rapsody">Rapsody</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Flo_Milli" title="Flo Milli">Flo Milli</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> as well as rock artist <a href="/wiki/Jack_White" title="Jack White">Jack White</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Also <a href="/wiki/Dotdash" class="mw-redirect" title="Dotdash">About.com</a> ranked her <abbr title="number">No.</abbr>&#160;26 on their list of the 50 Greatest MCs of Our Time (1987–2007)<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> and <abbr title="number">No.</abbr>&#160;6 in the Greatest Rappers Ever survey organized by <a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, <a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)"><i>Vibe</i> magazine</a> has referred to MC Lyte as the "<a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">Queen of Rap</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MC_Lyte&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2016, producer and rapper <a href="/wiki/Q-Tip_(musician)" title="Q-Tip (musician)">Q-Tip</a> revealed on his <a href="/wiki/Apple_Music_1" title="Apple Music 1">Apple Music 1</a> show <i>Abstract Radio</i> that he used to date Lyte in his days before landing a record deal with <a href="/wiki/A_Tribe_Called_Quest" title="A Tribe Called Quest">A Tribe Called Quest</a>. In the early 1990s, Lyte was in a relationship with Todd "Todd 1" Brown (1970-2019), then the producer of <i><a href="/wiki/Yo!_MTV_Raps" title="Yo! MTV Raps">Yo!
